         </a>

      <p>
       <b>
        Isabella I
       </b>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="es" xml:lang="es">
         Isabel
        </span>
       </i>
       , 22 April 1451 – 26 November 1504) was
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_of_Castile" title="Queen of Castile">
        Queen of Castile
       </a>
       from 1474 until her death. Her marriage to
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">
        Ferdinand II of Aragon
       </a>
       became the basis for the political unification of Spain under their grandson,
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">
        Charles I
       </a>
       . After a struggle to claim her right to the throne, she reorganized the governmental system, brought the crime rate to the lowest it had been in years, and unburdened the kingdom of the enormous debt her brother had left behind. Her reforms and those she made with her husband had an influence that extended well beyond the borders of their united kingdoms. Isabella and Ferdinand are known for completing the
       <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
        Reconquista
       </a>
       , ordering conversion or exile of their Muslim and Jewish subjects, and for supporting and financing
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       's
       <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus#First_voyage" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">
        1492 voyage
       </a>
       that led to the opening of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">
        New World
       </a>
       and to the establishment of
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       as the first global power which dominated Europe and much of the world for more than a century. Isabella, granted together with her husband the title "the Catholic" by Pope
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_VI" title="Pope Alexander VI">
        Alexander VI
       </a>
       , was recognized as a
       <a href="/wiki/Servant_of_God" title="Servant of God">
        Servant of God
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Catholic Church
       </a>
       in 1974.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4">
           <a href="#War_with_Portugal">

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Life_and_reign">
        Life and reign
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Life and reign">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">
        Early years
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Isabella was born in
       <a href="/wiki/Madrigal_de_las_Altas_Torres" title="Madrigal de las Altas Torres">
        Madrigal de las Altas Torres
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%81vila_(province)" title="Ávila (province)">
        Ávila
       </a>
       , to
       <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Castile" title="John II of Castile">
        John II of Castile
       </a>
       and his second wife,
       <a href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Portugal,_Queen_of_Castile" title="Isabella of Portugal, Queen of Castile">
        Isabella of Portugal
       </a>
       on 22 April 1451.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the time of her birth, she was second in line to the throne after her older half-brother
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_Castile" title="Henry IV of Castile">
        Henry IV of Castile
       </a>
       . Henry was 26 at that time and married, but childless. Her younger brother
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_of_Castile,_Prince_of_Asturias" title="Alfonso of Castile, Prince of Asturias">
        Alfonso of Castile
       </a>
       was born two years later on 17 November 1453, lowering her position to third in line.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When her father died in 1454, her half-brother ascended to the throne as King Henry IV of Castile. Isabella and her brother Alfonso were left in King Henry's care.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prescott,_William_1860,_p._28_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Prescott,_William_1860,_p._28-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She, her mother, and Alfonso then moved to
       <a href="/wiki/Ar%C3%A9valo" title="Arévalo">
        Arévalo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prescott,_William_1860,_p._83_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Prescott,_William_1860,_p._83-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       These were times of turmoil for Isabella. The living conditions at their castle in Arévalo were poor, and they suffered from a shortage of money. Although her father arranged in his will for his children to be financially well taken care of, King Henry did not comply with their father's wishes, either from a desire to keep his half-siblings restricted, or from ineptitude.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prescott,_William_1860,_p._28_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Prescott,_William_1860,_p._28-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Even though living conditions were difficult, under the careful eye of her mother, Isabella was instructed in lessons of practical piety and in a deep reverence for religion.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prescott,_William_1860,_p._83_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Prescott,_William_1860,_p._83-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       When the King's wife,
       <a href="/wiki/Joan_of_Portugal" title="Joan of Portugal">
        Joan of Portugal
       </a>
       , was about to give birth to their daughter
       <a href="/wiki/Joanna_la_Beltraneja" title="Joanna la Beltraneja">
        Joanna
       </a>
       , Isabella and her brother Alfonso were summoned to court in
       <a href="/wiki/Segovia" title="Segovia">
        Segovia
       </a>
       to come under the direct supervision of the King and to finish their education. Alfonso was placed in the care of a tutor while Isabella became part of the Queen's household.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isabel_de_castilla.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="368" data-file-width="195" height="321" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Isabel_de_castilla.jpg/170px-Isabel_de_castilla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/23/Isabel_de_castilla.jpg 1.5x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Isabel_de_castilla.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Isabella in the
         <i>
          Rimado de la Conquista de Granada
         </i>
         , from 1482, by Pedro Marcuello
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Some of Isabella's living conditions improved in Segovia. She always had food and clothing and lived in a castle that was adorned with gold and silver. Isabella's basic education consisted of reading, spelling, writing, grammar, mathematics, art, chess, dancing, embroidery, music, and religious instruction. She and her ladies-in-waiting entertained themselves with art, embroidery, and music. She lived a relaxed lifestyle, but she rarely left Segovia since King Henry forbade this. Her half-brother was keeping her from the political turmoils going on in the kingdom, though Isabella had full knowledge of what was going on and of her role in the feuds.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2018)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The noblemen, anxious for power, confronted King Henry, demanding that his younger half-brother Infante Alfonso be named his successor. They even went so far as to ask Alfonso to seize the throne. The nobles, now in control of Alfonso and claiming that he was the true heir, clashed with King Henry's forces at the
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Olmedo" title="Second Battle of Olmedo">
        Second Battle of Olmedo
       </a>
       in 1467. The battle was a draw. King Henry agreed to recognize Alfonso as his heir presumptive, provided that he would marry his daughter, Princess Joanna la Beltraneja.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Soon after he was named
       <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias" title="Prince of Asturias">
        Prince of Asturias
       </a>
       , Isabella's younger brother Alfonso died in July 1468, likely of the plague. The nobles who had supported him suspected poisoning. As she had been named in her brother's will as his successor, the nobles asked Isabella to take his place as champion of the rebellion. However, support for the rebels had begun to wane, and Isabella preferred a negotiated settlement to continuing the war.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She met with her elder brother Henry at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toros_de_Guisando" title="Toros de Guisando">
        Toros de Guisando
       </a>
       and they reached a compromise: the war would stop, King Henry would name Isabella his heir-presumptive instead of his daughter Joanna, and Isabella would not marry without her brother's consent, but he would not be able to force her to marry against her will.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plunkett_1915,_p._68_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plunkett_1915,_p._68-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Isabella's side came out with most of what the nobles desired, though they did not go so far as to officially depose King Henry; they were not powerful enough to do so, and Isabella did not want to jeopardize the principle of fair inherited succession, since it was upon this idea that she had based her argument for legitimacy as heir-presumptive.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">
        Marriage
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Marriage">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The question of Isabella's marriage was not a new one, she had made her debut in the matrimonial market at the tender age of six with a betrothal to
       <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">
        Ferdinand
       </a>
       , the younger son of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_II_of_Aragon" title="John II of Aragon">
        John II of Aragon
       </a>
       (whose family was a cadet branch of the
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Trast%C3%A1mara" title="House of Trastámara">
        House of Trastámara
       </a>
       ). At that time, the two kings, Henry and John, were eager to show their mutual love and confidence and they believed that this double alliance would make their eternal friendship obvious to the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This arrangement, however, did not last long.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fernando_e_Isabel.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="351" data-file-width="450" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Fernando_e_Isabel.jpg/220px-Fernando_e_Isabel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Fernando_e_Isabel.jpg/330px-Fernando_e_Isabel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Fernando_e_Isabel.jpg/440px-Fernando_e_Isabel.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fernando_e_Isabel.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The wedding portrait of Ferdinand and Isabella,
         <abbr title="circa">
          c.
         </abbr>
         1469.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Ferdinand's uncle
       <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_V_of_Aragon" title="Alfonso V of Aragon">
        Alfonso V of Aragon
       </a>
       died in 1458. All of Alfonso's Spanish territories, as well as the islands of Sicily and Sardinia, were left to his brother John II. John now had a stronger position than ever before and no longer needed the security of Henry's friendship. Henry was now in need of a new alliance. He saw the chance for this much needed new friendship in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Navarre" title="Charles IV of Navarre">
        Charles of Viana
       </a>
       , John's elder son.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Charles was constantly at odds with his father, and because of this, he secretly entered into an alliance with Henry IV of Castile. A major part of the alliance was that a marriage was to be arranged between Charles and Isabella. When John II learned of this arranged marriage he was outraged. Isabella had been intended for his favourite younger son, Ferdinand, and in his eyes this alliance was still valid. John II had his son Charles thrown in prison on charges of plotting against his father's life; Charles died in 1461.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isabel_I_of_Castile.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="877" data-file-width="626" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Isabel_I_of_Castile.jpg/220px-Isabel_I_of_Castile.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Isabel_I_of_Castile.jpg/330px-Isabel_I_of_Castile.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Isabel_I_of_Castile.jpg/440px-Isabel_I_of_Castile.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Isabel_I_of_Castile.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Isabella I of Castile
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1465, an attempt was made to marry Isabella to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_V_of_Portugal" title="Alfonso V of Portugal">
        Alfonso V of Portugal
       </a>
       , Henry's brother-in-law. Through the medium of the Queen and Count of Ledesma, a Portuguese alliance was made.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlckWell2000_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BlckWell2000-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Isabella, however, was wary of the marriage and refused to consent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       A civil war broke out in Castile over King Henry's inability to act as sovereign. Henry now needed a quick way to please the rebels of the kingdom. As part of an agreement to restore peace, Isabella was to be betrothed to
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Gir%C3%B3n_Acu%C3%B1a_Pacheco" title="Pedro Girón Acuña Pacheco">
        Pedro Girón Acuña Pacheco
       </a>
       , Master of the
       <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Calatrava" title="Order of Calatrava">
        Order of Calatrava
       </a>
       and brother to the King's favourite,
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pacheco" title="Juan Pacheco">
        Juan Pacheco
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlckWell2000_13-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-BlckWell2000-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In return, Don Pedro would pay into the impoverished royal treasury an enormous sum of money. Seeing no alternative, Henry agreed to the marriage. Isabella was aghast and prayed to God that the marriage would not come to pass. Her prayers were answered when Don Pedro suddenly fell ill and died while on his way to meet his fiancée.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlckWell2000_13-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-BlckWell2000-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       When Henry recognised Isabella as his heir-presumptive on 19 September 1468, he also promised that his sister should not be compelled to marry against her will, while she in return agreed to obtain his consent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plunkett_1915,_p._68_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plunkett_1915,_p._68-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It seemed that finally the years of failed attempts at political marriages were over. There was talk of a marriage to
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_IV_of_England" title="Edward IV of England">
        Edward IV of England
       </a>
       or to one of his brothers, probably
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_III_of_England" title="Richard III of England">
        Richard, Duke of Gloucester
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but this alliance was never seriously considered.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plunkett_1915,_p._68_9-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plunkett_1915,_p._68-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Once again in 1468, a marriage proposal arrived from Alfonso V of Portugal. Going against his promises made in September, Henry tried to make the marriage a reality. If Isabella married Alfonso, Henry's daughter Joanna would marry Alfonso's son
       <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">
        John II
       </a>
       and thus, after the death of the old king, John and Joanna could inherit Portugal and Castile.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Isabella refused and made a secret promise to marry her cousin and very first betrothed, Ferdinand of Aragon.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:IsabellaofCastile05.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="558" data-file-width="330" height="287" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/IsabellaofCastile05.jpg/170px-IsabellaofCastile05.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/IsabellaofCastile05.jpg/255px-IsabellaofCastile05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a1/IsabellaofCastile05.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:IsabellaofCastile05.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ferdinand and Isabella
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After this failed attempt, Henry once again went against his promises and tried to marry Isabella to
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_XI_of_France" title="Louis XI of France">
        Louis XI
       </a>
       's brother
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charles_de_Valois,_Duc_de_Berry" title="Charles de Valois, Duc de Berry">
        Charles, Duke of Berry
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In Henry's eyes, this alliance would cement the friendship of Castile and France as well as remove Isabella from Castilian affairs. Isabella once again refused the proposal. Meanwhile, John II of Aragon negotiated in secret with Isabella a wedding to his son Ferdinand.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On 18 October 1469, the formal betrothal took place.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plunkett_1915,_p._78_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plunkett_1915,_p._78-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because Isabella and Ferdinand were second cousins, they stood within the prohibited degrees of
       <a href="/wiki/Consanguinity" title="Consanguinity">
        consanguinity
       </a>
       and the marriage would not be legal unless a dispensation from the Pope was obtained.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With the help of the Valencian Cardinal Rodrigo Borgia (later
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_VI" title="Pope Alexander VI">
        Alexander VI
       </a>
       ), Isabella and Ferdinand were presented with a supposed papal bull by
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_II" title="Pope Pius II">
        Pius II
       </a>
       (who had died in 1464), authorising Ferdinand to marry within the third degree of consanguinity, making their marriage legal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plunkett_1915,_p._78_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plunkett_1915,_p._78-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Afraid of opposition, Isabella eloped from the court of Henry with the excuse of visiting her brother Alfonso's tomb in
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81vila,_Spain" title="Ávila, Spain">
        Ávila
       </a>
       . Ferdinand, on the other hand, crossed Castile in secret disguised as a servant. They were married immediately upon reuniting, on 19 October 1469, in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Audiencia_and_Chanciller%C3%ADa_of_Valladolid" title="Royal Audiencia and Chancillería of Valladolid">
        Palacio de los Vivero
       </a>
       in the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Valladolid" title="Valladolid">
        Valladolid
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gerli219_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Gerli219-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="War_with_Portugal">
        War with Portugal
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: War with Portugal">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Toro" title="Battle of Toro">
        Battle of Toro
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guinea" title="Battle of Guinea">
        Battle of Guinea
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Castilian_Succession" title="War of the Castilian Succession">
        War of the Castilian Succession
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       On 12 December 1474, news of Isabella's brother King Henry IV's death in
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
        Madrid
       </a>
       reached
       <a href="/wiki/Segovia" title="Segovia">
        Segovia
       </a>
       prompting Isabella to take refuge within the walls of the
       <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Segovia" title="Alcázar of Segovia">
        Alcázar of Segovia
       </a>
       where she received the support of Andres Cabrera and Segovia's council. The next day, Isabella was crowned as
       <b>
        Queen of Castile and León
       </b>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella's reign got off to a rocky start. Because her brother had named Isabella as his successor, when she ascended to the throne in 1474, there were already several plots against her.
       <a href="/wiki/Diego_Lopez_de_Pacheco,_2nd_Duke_of_Escalona" title="Diego Lopez de Pacheco, 2nd Duke of Escalona">
        Diego Pacheco
       </a>
       , the Marquis of Villena, and his followers maintained that
       <a href="/wiki/Joanna_la_Beltraneja" title="Joanna la Beltraneja">
        Joanna la Beltraneja
       </a>
       , daughter of King Henry IV, was the rightful queen.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Shortly after the Marquis made his claim, a longtime supporter of Isabella, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_Carillo_de_Acu%C3%B1a" title="Alfonso Carillo de Acuña">
        Archbishop of Toledo
       </a>
       , left court to plot with his great-nephew the Marquis. The Archbishop and Marquis made plans to have the Infanta Joanna marry her uncle,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfonso_V_of_Portugal" title="Alfonso V of Portugal">
        King Alfonso V of Portugal
       </a>
       and invade Castile to claim the throne for themselves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In May 1475, King Alfonso and his army crossed into Spain and advanced to
       <a href="/wiki/Plasencia" title="Plasencia">
        Plasencia
       </a>
       . Here he married the young Joanna.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A long and bloody war for the Castilian succession then took place. The war went back and forth for almost a year until 1 March 1476, when the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Toro" title="Battle of Toro">
        Battle of Toro
       </a>
       took place, a battle in which both sides claimed victory
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spanish_historian_Ana_Carrasco_Manchado_(21)_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spanish_historian_Ana_Carrasco_Manchado_(21)-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spanish_historian_Cesáreo_Fernández_Duro_(22)_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spanish_historian_Cesáreo_Fernández_Duro_(22)-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and celebrated
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spanish_historian_Cesáreo_Fernández_Duro_(22)_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spanish_historian_Cesáreo_Fernández_Duro_(22)-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Manchado_(23)_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Manchado_(23)-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the victory: the troops of King Alfonso V were beaten
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pulgar_(24)_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Pulgar_(24)-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garcia_de_Resende_(25)_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Garcia_de_Resende_(25)-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       by the Castilian centre-left commanded by the Duke of Alba and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_Mendoza" title="Cardinal Mendoza">
        Cardinal Mendoza
       </a>
       while the forces led by
       <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">
        Prince John of Portugal
       </a>
       defeated
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chronicler_Pulgar_(Castilian)_(26)_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Chronicler_Pulgar_(Castilian)_(26)-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronicler_Garcia_de_Resende_(Portuguese)(27)_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-chronicler_Garcia_de_Resende_(Portuguese)(27)-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronicler_Juan_de_Mariana_(Castilian)_(28)_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-chronicler_Juan_de_Mariana_(Castilian)_(28)-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronicler_Damião_de_Góis_(Portuguese)_(29)_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-chronicler_Damião_de_Góis_(Portuguese)_(29)-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the Castilian right wing and remained in possession
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronicler_Juan_de_Mariana_(Castilian)_(30)_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-chronicler_Juan_de_Mariana_(Castilian)_(30)-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chronicler_Rui_de_Pina_(Portuguese)_(31)_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-chronicler_Rui_de_Pina_(Portuguese)_(31)-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       of the battlefield.
      </p>
      <p>
       But despite its uncertain
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_historian_(32)_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-French_historian_(32)-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-French_historian_Joseph-Louis_Desormeaux_(33)_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-French_historian_Joseph-Louis_Desormeaux_(33)-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       outcome, the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Toro" title="Battle of Toro">
        Battle of Toro
       </a>
       represented a great political victory
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spanish_academic_António_M._(34)_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spanish_academic_António_M._(34)-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A._Ballesteros_Beretta_(35)_40-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-A._Ballesteros_Beretta_(35)-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vicente_Álvarez_Palenzuela_(36)_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Vicente_Álvarez_Palenzuela_(36)-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Spanish_academic_Rafael_Dominguez_(37)_42-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Spanish_academic_Rafael_Dominguez_(37)-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       for the
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">
        Catholic Monarchs
       </a>
       , assuring them the throne since the supporters of Joanna la Beltraneja disbanded and the Portuguese army, without allies, left Castile. As summarised by the historian
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Justo_Gonzalez" title="Justo Gonzalez">
        Justo L. González
       </a>
       :
      </p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>
        Both armies faced each other at the camps of Toro resulting in an indecisive battle. But while the Portuguese King reorganised his troops, Ferdinand sent news to all the cities of Castile and to several foreign kingdoms informing them about a huge victory where the Portuguese were crushed. Faced with these news, the party of "la Beltraneja"
        <i>
         [Joanna]
        </i>
        was dissolved and the Portuguese were forced to return to their kingdom.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Justo_L._González_(38)_43-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Justo_L._González_(38)-43">
          [43]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </p>
      </blockquote>
      <p>
       With great political vision, Isabella took advantage of the moment and convoked courts at Madrigal-Segovia (April–October 1476)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historian_Marvin_44-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Historian_Marvin-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       where her eldest child and daughter
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Aragon_and_Castile" title="Isabella of Aragon and Castile">
        Isabella
       </a>
       was firstly sworn as heiress to Castile's crown. That was equivalent to legitimising Isabella's own throne.
      </p>
      <p>
       In August of the same year, Isabella proved her abilities as a powerful ruler on her own. A rebellion broke out in Segovia, and Isabella rode out to suppress it, as her husband Ferdinand was off fighting at the time. Going against the advice of her male advisors, Isabella rode by herself into the city to negotiate with the rebels. She was successful and the rebellion was quickly brought to an end.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two years later, Isabella further secured her place as ruler with the birth of her son
       <a href="/wiki/John,_Prince_of_Asturias" title="John, Prince of Asturias">
        John, Prince of Asturias
       </a>
       , on 30 June 1478. To many, the presence of a male heir legitimised her place as ruler.
      </p>
      <p>
       Meanwhile, the Castilian and Portuguese fleets fought for hegemony in the Atlantic Ocean and for the wealth of Guinea (gold and slaves), where the decisive naval
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guinea" title="Battle of Guinea">
        Battle of Guinea
       </a>
       was fought.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Battle_of_Guinea_(40)_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Battle_of_Guinea_(40)-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Historian_Malyn_Newitt_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Historian_Malyn_Newitt-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The war dragged on for another three years
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and ended with a Castilian victory on land
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bailey_W._Diffie_(42)_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bailey_W._Diffie_(42)-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and a Portuguese victory on the sea.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bailey_W._Diffie_(42)_49-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bailey_W._Diffie_(42)-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The four separate peace treaties signed at
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Alc%C3%A1%C3%A7ovas" title="Treaty of Alcáçovas">
        Alcáçovas
       </a>
       (4 September 1479) reflected that result: Portugal gave up the throne of Castile in favour of Isabella in exchange for a very favourable share of the Atlantic territories disputed with Castile (they all went to Portugal with the exception of the
       <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">
        Canary Islands
       </a>
       :
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Alonso_de_Palencia_(44)_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Alonso_de_Palencia_(44)-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Guinea" title="Gulf of Guinea">
        Guinea
       </a>
       with its mines of gold,
       <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">
        Cape Verde
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">
        Madeira
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">
        Azores
       </a>
       , and the right of conquest over the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Fez" title="Kingdom of Fez">
        Kingdom of Fez
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) plus a large war compensation: 106.676 dobles of gold.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mendonça_(47)_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mendonça_(47)-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Catholic Monarchs also had to accept that Joanna la Beltraneja remain in Portugal instead of Spain
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mendonça_(47)_54-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mendonça_(47)-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and to pardon all rebellious subjects who had supported Joanna and King Alfonso.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edwards_2000,_p._38_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Edwards_2000,_p._38-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       And the Catholic Monarchs—who had proclaimed themselves rulers of Portugal and donated lands to noblemen inside this country
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       —had to give up the Portuguese crown.
      </p>
      <p>
       At Alcáçovas, Isabella and Ferdinand had conquered the throne, but the Portuguese exclusive right of navigation and commerce in all of the Atlantic Ocean south of the Canary Islands meant that Spain was practically blocked out of the Atlantic and was deprived of the gold of Guinea, which induced anger in
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Battle_of_Guinea_(40)_46-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Battle_of_Guinea_(40)-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spanish academic Antonio Rumeu de Armas claims that with the peace treaty of Alcáçovas in 1479, the Catholic Monarchs "...buy the peace at an excessively expensive price..."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-António_Rumeu_de_Armas_(49)_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-António_Rumeu_de_Armas_(49)-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and historian Mª Monserrat León Guerrero added that they "...find themselves forced to abandon their expansion by the Atlantic...".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mª_Monserrat_León_Guerrero_(50)_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mª_Monserrat_León_Guerrero_(50)-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       freed Castile from this difficult situation, because his New World discovery led to a new and much more balanced sharing of the Atlantic at Tordesillas in 1494. As the orders received by Columbus in his first voyage (1492) show: "[the Catholic Monarchs] have always in mind that the limits signed in the share of Alcáçovas should not be overcome, and thus they insist with Columbus to sail along the parallel of Canary."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mª_Monserrat_León_Guerrero_(50)_58-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mª_Monserrat_León_Guerrero_(50)-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Thus, by sponsoring the Columbian adventure to the west, the Spanish monarchs were trying the only remaining path of expansion. As is now known, they would be extremely successful on this issue. Isabella had proven herself to be a fighter and tough monarch from the start. Now that she had succeeded in securing her place on the Castilian throne, she could begin to institute the reforms that the kingdom desperately needed.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Reform">
        Reform
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Reform">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Regulation_of_crime">
        Regulation of crime
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Regulation of crime">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       When Isabella came to the throne in 1474, Castile was in a state of despair thanks to her brother Henry's reign. It was not unknown that Henry IV was a big spender and did little to enforce the laws of his kingdom. It was even said by one Castilian denizen of the time that murder, rape, and robbery happened without punishment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Because of this, Isabella needed desperately to find a way to reform her kingdom. Due to the measures imposed, historians during her lifetime saw her to be more inclined to justice than to mercy, and indeed far more rigorous and unforgiving than her husband Ferdinand.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="La_Santa_Hermandad">
        La Santa Hermandad
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: La Santa Hermandad">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hermandad" title="Hermandad">
        Hermandad
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Isabella's first major reform came during the cortes of Madrigal in 1476 in the form of a police force, La Santa Hermandad (the Holy Brotherhood). While 1476 was not the first time that Castile had seen the Hermandad, it was the first time that the police force was used by the crown.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During the late medieval period, the expression
       <i>
        hermandad
       </i>
       had been used to describe groups of men who came together of their own accord to regulate law and order by patrolling the roads and countryside and punishing malefactors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These brotherhoods had usually been suppressed by the monarch, however. Before 1476, the justice system in most parts of the country was effectively under the control of dissident members of the nobility rather than royal officials.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       To fix this problem, during 1476, a general Hermandad was established for Castile,
       <a href="/wiki/Le%C3%B3n_(historical_region)" title="León (historical region)">
        Leon
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Asturias" title="Asturias">
        Asturias
       </a>
       . The police force was to be made up of locals who were to regulate the crime occurring in the kingdom. It was to be paid for by a tax of 1800
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Maraved%C3%ADs&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Maravedís (page does not exist)">
        maravedís
       </a>
       on every one hundred households.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1477, Isabella visited
       <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">
        Extremadura
       </a>
       and Andalusia to introduce this more efficient police force there as well.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h5>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_criminal_reforms">
        Other criminal reforms
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Other criminal reforms">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h5>
      <p>
       Keeping with her reformation of the regulation of laws, in 1481 Isabella charged two officials with restoring peace in
       <a href="/wiki/Galicia_(Spain)" title="Galicia (Spain)">
        Galicia
       </a>
       . This turbulent province had been the prey of tyrant nobles since the days of Isabella's father, John II.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Robbers infested the highways and oppressed the smaller towns and villages. These officials set off with the Herculean task of restoring peace for the province. The officials were successful. They succeeded in driving over 1,500 robbers from Galicia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">
        Finances
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Finances">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       From the very beginning of her reign, Isabella fully grasped the importance of restoring the Crown's finances. The reign of Henry IV had left the kingdom of Castile in great debt. Upon examination, it was found that the chief cause of the nation's poverty was the wholesale alienation of royal estates during Henry's reign.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plunkett_1915,_p._150_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plunkett_1915,_p._150-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       To make money, Henry had sold off royal estates at prices well below their value. The Cortes of Toledo of 1480 came to the conclusion that the only hope of lasting financial reform lay in a resumption of these alienated lands and rents. This decision was warmly approved by many leading nobles of the court, but Isabella was reluctant to take such drastic measures. It was decided that the Cardinal of Spain would hold an enquiry into the tenure of estates and rents acquired during Henry IV's reign. Those that had not been granted as a reward for services were to be restored without compensation, while those that had been sold at a price far below their real value were to be bought back at the same sum. While many of the nobility were forced to pay large sums of money for their estates, the royal treasury became ever richer. Isabella's one stipulation was that there would be no revocation of gifts made to churches, hospitals, or the poor.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
        <a href="#cite_note-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Another issue of money was the overproduction of coinage and the abundance of mints in the kingdom. During Henry's reign, the number of mints regularly producing money had increased from just five to 150.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Plunkett_1915,_p._150_68-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Plunkett_1915,_p._150-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Much of the coinage produced in these mints was nearly worthless. During the first year of her reign, Isabella established a monopoly over the royal mints and fixed a legal standard to which the coinage must approximate. By shutting down many of the mints and taking royal control over the production of money, Isabella restored the confidence of the public in the Crown's ability to handle the kingdom's finance.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government">
        Government
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Both Isabella and Ferdinand established very few new governmental and administrative institutions in their respective kingdoms. Especially in Castile, the main achievement was to use more effectively the institutions that had existed during the reigns of John II and Henry IV.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Historically, the center of the Castilian government had been the royal household, together with its surrounding court. The household was traditionally divided into two overlapping bodies. The first body was made up of household officials, mainly people of the nobility, who carried out governmental and political functions for which they received special payment. The second body was made up of some 200 permanent servants or
       <i>
        continos
       </i>
       who performed a wide range of confidential functions on behalf of the rulers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the 1470s, when Isabella began to take a firm grip on the royal administration, the senior offices of the royal household were simply honorary titles and held strictly by the nobility. The positions of a more secretarial nature were often held by senior churchmen. Substantial revenues were attached to such offices and were therefore enjoyed greatly, on an effectively hereditary basis, by the great Castilian houses of nobility. While the nobles held the titles, individuals of lesser breeding did the real work.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Losreyescatolicos.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="278" data-file-width="424" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Losreyescatolicos.jpg/220px-Losreyescatolicos.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Losreyescatolicos.jpg/330px-Losreyescatolicos.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ac/Losreyescatolicos.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Losreyescatolicos.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Ferdinand and Isabella with their subjects
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Traditionally, the main advisory body to the rulers of Castile was the
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Castile" title="Council of Castile">
        Royal Council
       </a>
       . The Council, under the monarch, had full power to resolve all legal and political disputes. The Council was responsible for supervising all senior administrative officials, such as the Crown representatives in all of the major towns. It was also the supreme judicial tribunal of the kingdom.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1480, during the Cortes of Toledo, Isabella made many reforms to the Royal Council. Previously there had been two distinct yet overlapping categories of royal councillor. One formed a group which possessed both judicial and administrative responsibilities. This portion consisted of some bishops, some nobles, and an increasingly important element of professional administrators with legal training known as
       <i>
        letrados
       </i>
       . The second category of traditional councillor had a less formal role. This role depended greatly on the individuals' political influence and personal influence with the monarch. During Isabella's reign, the role of this second category was completely eliminated.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As mentioned previously, Isabella had little care for personal bribes or favours. Because of this, this second type of councillor, usually of the nobility, was only allowed to attend the council of Castile as an observer.
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella began to rely more on the professional administrators than ever before. These men were mostly of the
       <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">
        bourgeoisie
       </a>
       or lesser nobility. The Council was also rearranged and it was officially settled that one bishop, three
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Knight" title="Knight">
         caballeros
        </a>
       </i>
       , and eight or nine lawyers would serve on the council at a time. While the nobles were no longer directly involved in the matters of state, they were welcome to attend the meetings. Isabella hoped by forcing the nobility to choose whether to participate or not would weed out those who were not dedicated to the state and its cause.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella also saw the need to provide a personal relationship between herself as the monarch and her subjects. Therefore, Isabella and Ferdinand set aside a time every Friday during which they themselves would sit and allow people to come to them with complaints. This was a new form of personal justice that Castile had not seen before. The Council of State was reformed and presided over by the King and Queen. This department of public affairs dealt mainly with foreign negotiations, hearing embassies, and transacting business with the Court of Rome. In addition to these departments, there was also a Supreme Court of the Santa Hermandad, a Council of Finance, and a Council for settling purely Aragonese matters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although Isabella made many reforms that seem to have made the Cortes stronger, in actuality the Cortes lost political power during the reigns of Isabella and Ferdinand. Isabella and her husband moved in the direction of a non-parliamentary government and the Cortes became an almost passive advisory body, giving automatic assent to legislation which had been drafted by the royal administration.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After the reforms of the Cortes of Toledo, the Queen ordered a noted jurist, Alfonso Diaz de Montalvo, to undertake the task of clearing away legal rubbish and compiling what remained into a comprehensive code. Within four years the work stood completed in eight bulky volumes and the Ordenanzas Reales took their place on legal bookshelves.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
        <a href="#cite_note-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Events_of_1492">
        Events of 1492
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Events of 1492">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Granada">
        Granada
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Granada">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Isabella_by_Bigarny01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="760" data-file-width="742" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Isabella_by_Bigarny01.jpg/220px-Isabella_by_Bigarny01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Isabella_by_Bigarny01.jpg/330px-Isabella_by_Bigarny01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Isabella_by_Bigarny01.jpg/440px-Isabella_by_Bigarny01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Isabella_by_Bigarny01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Statue of Isabella by
         <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Bigarny" title="Felipe Bigarny">
          Felipe Bigarny
         </a>
         ; it resides in the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capilla_Real_de_Granada" title="Capilla Real de Granada">
          Capilla Real
         </a>
         , in
         <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
          Granada
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       At the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
        Reconquista
       </a>
       , only Granada was left for Isabella and Ferdinand to conquer. The
       <a href="/wiki/Emirate_of_Granada" title="Emirate of Granada">
        Emirate of Granada
       </a>
       had been held by the Muslim
       <a href="/wiki/Nasrid_dynasty" title="Nasrid dynasty">
        Nasrid
       </a>
       dynasty since the mid-13th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
        <a href="#cite_note-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Protected by natural barriers and fortified towns, it had withstood the long process of the
       <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">
        reconquista
       </a>
       . On 1 February 1482, the king and queen reached
       <a href="/wiki/Medina_del_Campo" title="Medina del Campo">
        Medina del Campo
       </a>
       and this is generally considered the beginning of the war for Granada. While Isabella's and Ferdinand's involvement in the war was apparent from the start, Granada's leadership was divided and never able to present a united front.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It still took ten years to conquer Granada, however, culminating in 1492.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Spanish monarchs recruited soldiers from many European countries and improved their artillery with the latest and best cannons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Systematically, they proceeded to take the kingdom piece by piece. In 1485 they laid siege to
       <a href="/wiki/Ronda" title="Ronda">
        Ronda
       </a>
       , which surrendered after only a fortnight due to extensive bombardment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
        <a href="#cite_note-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The following year,
       <a href="/wiki/Loja,_Granada" title="Loja, Granada">
        Loja
       </a>
       was taken, and again
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_XII_of_Granada" title="Muhammad XII of Granada">
        Muhammad XII
       </a>
       was captured and released. One year later, with the fall of
       <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="Málaga">
        Málaga
       </a>
       , the western part of the Muslim
       <a href="/wiki/Nasrid_dynasty" title="Nasrid dynasty">
        Nasrid
       </a>
       kingdom had fallen into Spanish hands. The eastern province succumbed after the fall of
       <a href="/wiki/Baza,_Granada" title="Baza, Granada">
        Baza
       </a>
       in 1489. The siege of Granada began in the spring of 1491 and at the end of the year, Muhammad XII surrendered. On 2 January 1492 Isabella and Ferdinand entered Granada to receive the keys of the city, and the principal
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Cordoba" title="Great Mosque of Cordoba">
        mosque
       </a>
       was reconsecrated as a church.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Granada" title="Treaty of Granada">
        Treaty of Granada
       </a>
       was signed later that year, and in it Ferdinand and Isabella gave their word to allow the Muslims and Jews of Granada to live in peace. An uprising by the
       <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">
        Moors
       </a>
       in 1500 caused the Catholic side to consider that the Moors had violated the Treaty: this gave them a justification for revoking its provisions. See
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morisco_Revolt" title="Morisco Revolt">
        Morisco Revolt
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       During the war, Isabella noted the abilities and energy of
       <a href="/wiki/Gonzalo_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Gonzalo Fernández de Córdoba">
        Gonzalo Fernández de Córdoba
       </a>
       and made him one of the two commissioners for the negotiations. Under her patronage, De Córdoba went on to an extraordinary military career that revolutionised the organisation and tactics of the emerging Spanish military, changing the nature of warfare and altering the European balance of power.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Columbus_and_Portuguese_relations">
        Columbus and Portuguese relations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Columbus and Portuguese relations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WC_Delacroix,Eugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="888" data-file-width="1168" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg/220px-WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg/330px-WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg/440px-WC_Delacroix%2CEugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WC_Delacroix,Eugene_The_Return_of_Christopher_Columbus.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The return of Christopher Columbus; his audience before King Ferdinand and Queen Isabella.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Just three months after entering Granada, Queen Isabella agreed to sponsor
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Christopher Columbus
       </a>
       on an expedition to reach the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indies" title="Indies">
        Indies
       </a>
       by sailing west (2000 miles, according to Columbus).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
        <a href="#cite_note-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The crown agreed to pay a sum of money as a concession from monarch to subject.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edwards,_John_2005,_p._120_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Edwards,_John_2005,_p._120-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       His expedition departed on 3 August 1492, and arrived in
       <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_Island" title="San Salvador Island">
        San Salvador Island
       </a>
       on 12 October. He named it San Salvador after Jesus the Savior.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edwards,_John_2005,_p._120_85-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Edwards,_John_2005,_p._120-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He returned the next year and presented his findings to the monarchs, bringing natives and gold under a hero's welcome. Although Columbus was sponsored by the Castilian queen, treasury accounts show no royal payments to him until 1493, after his first voyage was complete.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
        <a href="#cite_note-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spain entered a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Age_(metaphor)" title="Golden Age (metaphor)">
        Golden Age
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">
        exploration
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">
        colonisation
       </a>
       , the period of the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        Spanish Empire
       </a>
       . The Portuguese did not recognise that South America belonged to the Spanish because it was in Portugal's sphere of influence, and the Portuguese King John II threatened to send an army to claim the land for the Portuguese. In 1494, by the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">
        Treaty of Tordesillas
       </a>
       , Isabella and Ferdinand agreed to divide the Earth, outside of Europe, with king
       <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">
        John II
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Portugal" title="Kingdom of Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella was not in favour of Columbus' enslavement of the
       <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
        American natives
       </a>
       and attempted to enforce the recent policies of the
       <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">
        Canaries
       </a>
       upon the 'New World', stating that all peoples were under the subject of the Castilian Crown and could not be enslaved in most situations. The principles she established would have very little effect during her lifetime, however.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tame08_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tame08-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Expulsion_of_the_Jews">
        Expulsion of the Jews
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Expulsion of the Jews">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_Decree" title="Alhambra Decree">
        Alhambra Decree
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">
        Spanish Inquisition
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       With the institution of the Roman Catholic Inquisition in Spain, and with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dominican_friar" title="Dominican friar">
        Dominican friar
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1s_de_Torquemada" title="Tomás de Torquemada">
        Tomás de Torquemada
       </a>
       as the first Inquisitor General, the Catholic Monarchs pursued a policy of religious and national unity. Though Isabella opposed taking harsh measures against Jews on economic grounds, Torquemada was able to convince Ferdinand.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2013)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       On 31 March 1492, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alhambra_decree" title="Alhambra decree">
        Alhambra decree
       </a>
       for the expulsion of the Jews was issued.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liss_1992._p._298_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Liss_1992._p._298-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Jews had until the end of July, three months, to leave the country and they were not to take with them gold, silver, money, arms, or horses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Liss_1992._p._298_88-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Liss_1992._p._298-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Traditionally, it had been claimed that as many as 200,000 Jews left Spain, but recent historians have shown that such figures are exaggerated:
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Kamen" title="Henry Kamen">
        Henry Kamen
       </a>
       has shown that out of a total population of 80,000 Jews, a maximum of 40,000 left and the rest converted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hundreds of those that remained came under the Inquisition's investigations into relapsed
       <i>
        conversos
       </i>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marranos" title="Marranos">
        Marranos
       </a>
       ) and the Judaizers who had been abetting them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Later_years">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="vertical-navbox" style="float:right;clear:right;width:20em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;background: #FFFFFF; border-spacing: 0px; padding: 0px;">

        <td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%;padding-right: 5px;">
         <div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini">
          <ul>
           <li class="nv-view">
            <a href="/wiki/Template:House_of_Trast%C3%A1mara" title="Template:House of Trastámara">

              v
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-talk">
            <a href="/wiki/Template_talk:House_of_Trast%C3%A1mara" title="Template talk:House of Trastámara">
