              t
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
           <li class="nv-edit">
            <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:House_of_Trast%C3%A1mara&amp;action=edit">
             <abbr title="Edit this template">
              e
             </abbr>
            </a>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Isabella received the title of
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">
        Catholic Monarch
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_Alexander_VI" title="Pope Alexander VI">
        Pope Alexander VI
       </a>
       , a pope of whose behavior and involvement in matters Isabella did not approve. Along with the physical unification of Spain, Isabella and Ferdinand embarked on a process of spiritual unification, trying to bring the country under one faith (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       ). As part of this process, the Inquisition became institutionalised. After a Muslim uprising in 1499, and further troubles thereafter, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Granada" title="Treaty of Granada">
        Treaty of Granada
       </a>
       was broken in 1502, and Muslims were ordered to either become Christians or to leave. Isabella's confessor,
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Cisneros" title="Francisco Jiménez de Cisneros">
        Cisneros
       </a>
       , was named Archbishop of
       <a href="/wiki/Toledo,_Spain" title="Toledo, Spain">
        Toledo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       He was instrumental in a program of rehabilitation of the religious institutions of Spain, laying the groundwork for the later
       <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">
        Counter-Reformation
       </a>
       . As Chancellor, he exerted more and more power.
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella and her husband had created an
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
        empire
       </a>
       and in later years were consumed with administration and politics; they were concerned with the succession and worked to link the Spanish crown to the other rulers in Europe. By early 1497, all the pieces seemed to be in place: The son and heir
       <a href="/wiki/John,_Prince_of_Asturias" title="John, Prince of Asturias">
        John, Prince of Asturias
       </a>
       , married a Habsburg princess,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archduchess_Margaret_of_Austria" title="Archduchess Margaret of Austria">
        Margaret of Austria
       </a>
       , establishing the connection to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">
        Habsburgs
       </a>
       . The eldest daughter,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabella,_Princess_of_Asturias_(1470%E2%80%931498)" title="Isabella, Princess of Asturias (1470–1498)">
        Isabella of Aragon
       </a>
       , married
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">
        King Manuel I of Portugal
       </a>
       , and the younger daughter,
       <a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">
        Joanna of Castile
       </a>
       , was married to a Habsburg prince,
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_I_of_Castile" title="Philip I of Castile">
        Philip I of Habsburg
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       However, Isabella's plans for her eldest two children did not work out. Her only son, John of Asturias, died shortly after his marriage. Her daughter Isabella of Aragon, whose son
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miguel_da_Paz,_Prince_of_Asturias" title="Miguel da Paz, Prince of Asturias">
        Miguel da Paz
       </a>
       died at the age of two, died in childbirth. Queen Isabella I's crowns passed to her third child Joanna and her son-in-law, Philip I.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella did, however, make successful dynastic matches for her three youngest daughters. The death of Isabella of Aragon created a necessity for Manuel I of Portugal to remarry, and Isabella's third daughter,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_of_Aragon_and_Castile" title="Maria of Aragon and Castile">
        Maria of Aragon
       </a>
       , became his next bride. Isabella's youngest daughter,
       <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">
        Catherine of Aragon
       </a>
       , married England's
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Arthur, Prince of Wales">
        Arthur, Prince of Wales
       </a>
       , but his early death resulted in her being married to his younger brother,
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">
        King Henry VIII of England
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella officially withdrew from governmental affairs on September 14, 1504 and she died that same year on 26 November at the
       <a href="/wiki/Medina_del_Campo#Royal_Palace" title="Medina del Campo">
        Medina del Campo Royal Palace
       </a>
       . It is said that she had truly already been in decline since the death of her son Prince John of Asturias in 1497.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She is entombed in
       <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
        Granada
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capilla_Real_de_Granada" title="Capilla Real de Granada">
        Capilla Real
       </a>
       , which was built by her grandson,
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">
        Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor
       </a>
       (Carlos I of Spain), alongside her husband Ferdinand, her daughter Joanna and Joanna's husband Philip I; and Isabella's 2-year-old grandson, Miguel da Paz (the son of Isabella's daughter, also named Isabella, and King Manuel I of Portugal). The museum next to the Capilla Real holds her
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_(headgear)" title="Crown (headgear)">
        crown
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scepter" title="Scepter">
        scepter
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Appearance_and_personality">
        Appearance and personality
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Appearance and personality">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Reinaisabeldecastilla.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="481" height="271" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Reinaisabeldecastilla.jpg/170px-Reinaisabeldecastilla.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Reinaisabeldecastilla.jpg/255px-Reinaisabeldecastilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Reinaisabeldecastilla.jpg/340px-Reinaisabeldecastilla.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Reinaisabeldecastilla.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Isabella depicted with darker hair,
         <abbr title="circa">
          c.
         </abbr>
         1485
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Isabella was short but of strong stocky build, of a very fair complexion, and had a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hair_color" title="Hair color">
        hair color
       </a>
       that was between strawberry-blonde and
       <a href="/wiki/Auburn_hair" title="Auburn hair">
        auburn
       </a>
       . Some portraits, however, show her as a brunette. Her daughters, Joanna and Catherine, were thought to resemble her the most. Isabella maintained an austere, temperate lifestyle, and her religious spirit influenced her the most in life. In spite of her hostility towards the Muslims in
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusia
       </a>
       , Isabella developed a taste for Moorish decor and style. Of her, contemporaries said:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Oviedo" title="Fernández de Oviedo">
         Fernández de Oviedo
        </a>
        : "To see her speak was divine."
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Andr%C3%A9s_Bern%C3%A1ldez&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Andrés Bernáldez (page does not exist)">
         Andrés Bernáldez
        </a>
        <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
         (
         <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andr%C3%A9s_Bern%C3%A1ldez" title="es:Andrés Bernáldez">
          es
         </a>
         )
        </span>
        : "She was an endeavored woman, very powerful, very prudent, wise, very honest, chaste, devout, discreet, truthful, clear, without deceit. Who could count the excellences of this very Catholic and happy Queen, always very worthy of praises."
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Hernando_del_Pulgar" title="Hernando del Pulgar">
         Hernando del Pulgar
        </a>
        : "She was very inclined to justice, so much so that she was reputed to follow more the path of rigor than that of mercy, and did so to remedy the great corruption of crimes that she found in the kingdom when she succeeded to the throne."
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
         <a href="#cite_note-94">
          [94]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lucio_Marineo_S%C3%ADculo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lucio Marineo Sículo (page does not exist)">
         Lucio Marineo Sículo
        </a>
        <span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">
         (
         <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lucio_Marineo_S%C3%ADculo" title="es:Lucio Marineo Sículo">
          es
         </a>
         )
        </span>
        : "[The royal knight Alvaro Yáñez de Lugo] was condemned to be beheaded, although he offered forty thousand
        <i>
         ducados
        </i>
        for the war against the Moors to the court so that these monies spare his life. This matter was discussed with the queen, and there were some who told her to pardon him, since these funds for the war were better than the death of that man, and her highness should take them. But the queen, preferring justice to cash, very prudently refused them; and although she could have confiscated all his goods, which were many, she did not take any of them to avoid any note of greed, or that it be thought that she had not wished to pardon him in order to have his goods; instead, she gave them all to the children of the aforesaid knight."
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
         <a href="#cite_note-95">
          [95]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Ferdinand, in his testament, declared that "she was exemplary in all acts of virtue and of fear of God."
       </li>
       <li>
        Fray
        <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Jim%C3%A9nez_de_Cisneros" title="Francisco Jiménez de Cisneros">
         Francisco Jiménez de Cisneros
        </a>
        , her confessor, praised "her purity of heart, her big heart and the grandness of her soul".
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Family">
        Family
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Family">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>

         </div>
        </td>

           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Los_Reyes_Cat%C3%B3licos_y_la_infanta_do%C3%B1a_Juana.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="752" data-file-width="511" height="250" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Los_Reyes_Cat%C3%B3licos_y_la_infanta_do%C3%B1a_Juana.jpg/170px-Los_Reyes_Cat%C3%B3licos_y_la_infanta_do%C3%B1a_Juana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Los_Reyes_Cat%C3%B3licos_y_la_infanta_do%C3%B1a_Juana.jpg/255px-Los_Reyes_Cat%C3%B3licos_y_la_infanta_do%C3%B1a_Juana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Los_Reyes_Cat%C3%B3licos_y_la_infanta_do%C3%B1a_Juana.jpg/340px-Los_Reyes_Cat%C3%B3licos_y_la_infanta_do%C3%B1a_Juana.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Los_Reyes_Cat%C3%B3licos_y_la_infanta_do%C3%B1a_Juana.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Isabella and
         <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Ferdinand II of Aragon">
          Ferdinand
         </a>
         with their daughter,
         <a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">
          Joanna
         </a>
         ,
         <abbr title="circa">
          c.
         </abbr>
         1482.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Isabella and Ferdinand had five surviving children.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isabella_of_Aragon_and_Castile" title="Isabella of Aragon and Castile">
         Isabella
        </a>
        (1470–1498) married firstly to
        <a href="/wiki/Afonso,_Prince_of_Portugal" title="Afonso, Prince of Portugal">
         Alfonso, Prince of Portugal
        </a>
        , no issue. Married secondly to
        <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">
         Manuel I of Portugal
        </a>
        , no surviving issue.
       </li>
       <li>
        A son, miscarried on 31 May 1475 in
        <a href="/wiki/Cebreros" title="Cebreros">
         Cebreros
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Juan,_Prince_of_Asturias" title="Juan, Prince of Asturias">
         John
        </a>
        (1478–1497),
        <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias" title="Prince of Asturias">
         Prince of Asturias
        </a>
        . Married
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archduchess_Margaret_of_Austria" title="Archduchess Margaret of Austria">
         Archduchess Margaret of Austria
        </a>
        , no surviving issue.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">
         Joanna
        </a>
        (1479–1555),
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queen_of_Castile" title="Queen of Castile">
         Queen of Castile
        </a>
        . Married
        <a href="/wiki/Philip_I_of_Castile" title="Philip I of Castile">
         Philip the Handsome
        </a>
        , had issue.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_of_Aragon_and_Castile" title="Maria of Aragon and Castile">
         Maria
        </a>
        (1482–1517), married
        <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">
         Manuel I of Portugal
        </a>
        , her sister's widower, had issue.
       </li>
       <li>
        A stillborn daughter, twin of Maria. Born 1 July 1482 at dawn.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Catherine_of_Aragon" title="Catherine of Aragon">
         Catherine
        </a>
        (1485–1536), married firstly to
        <a href="/wiki/Arthur,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Arthur, Prince of Wales">
         Arthur, Prince of Wales
        </a>
        , no issue. Married his younger brother,
        <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII_of_England" title="Henry VIII of England">
         Henry VIII of England
        </a>
        and was mother of
        <a href="/wiki/Mary_I_of_England" title="Mary I of England">
         Mary I of England
        </a>
        .
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Towards the end of her life, family tragedies overwhelmed her, although she met these reverses with grace and fortitude. The death of her beloved son and heir and the miscarriage of his wife, the death of her daughter Isabella and Isabella's son Miguel (who could have united the kingdoms of the
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Monarchs" title="Catholic Monarchs">
        Catholic Monarchs
       </a>
       with that of Portugal), the madness of her daughter Joanna and the indifference of Philip the Handsome, and the uncertainty Catherine was in after the death of
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Arthur, Prince of Wales">
        her husband
       </a>
       submerged her in profound sadness that made her dress in black for the rest of her lifetime
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="Reliable source needed for the whole sentence (February 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . Her strong spirituality is well understood from the words she said after hearing of her son's death: "The Lord gave him to me, the Lord hath taken him from me, glory be His holy name."
      </p>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Descendants_of_Isabella_I_of_Castile_and_Ferdinand_II_of_Aragon" title="Descendants of Isabella I of Castile and Ferdinand II of Aragon">
        Descendants of Isabella I of Castile and Ferdinand II of Aragon
       </a>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sanctity">
        Sanctity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sanctity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       It is important to note that Isabella's reputation for sanctity derives in large measure from an image carefully shaped and disseminated by the queen herself.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1958, the
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Catholic
       </a>
       canonical
       <a href="/wiki/Beatification" title="Beatification">
        process of the Cause of Canonization
       </a>
       of Isabella was started by José García Goldaraz, the Bishop of Valladolid, where she died in 1504. 17 experts were appointed to investigate more than 100,000 documents in the archives of Spain and the
       <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">
        Vatican
       </a>
       and the merits of opening a canonical process of canonisation. 3,500 of these were chosen to be included in 27 volumes.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1970, the Commission determined that "A Canonical process for the canonization of Isabella the Catholic could be undertaken with a sense of security since there was not found one single act, public or private, of Queen Isabella that was not inspired by Christian and evangelical criteria; moreover there was a 'reputation of sanctity' uninterrupted for five centuries and as the investigation was progressing, it was more accentuated."
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1972, the Process of Valladolid was officially submitted to the
       <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_the_Causes_of_Saints" title="Congregation for the Causes of Saints">
        Congregation for the Causes of Saints
       </a>
       in the Vatican. This process was approved and Isabel was given the title "
       <a href="/wiki/Servant_of_God" title="Servant of God">
        Servant of God
       </a>
       " in March 1974.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-queenisabel.com_97-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-queenisabel.com-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Arms">
        Arms
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Arms">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       As
       <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Asturias" title="Prince of Asturias">
        Princess of Asturias
       </a>
       , Isabella bore the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Undifferenced_arms" title="Undifferenced arms">
        undifferenced
       </a>
       royal arms of the Crown of Castile and added the
       <a href="/wiki/Eagle_(heraldry)#Eagle_of_Saint_John" title="Eagle (heraldry)">
        Saint John the Evangelist's Eagle
       </a>
       , an
       <a href="/wiki/Eagle_(heraldry)" title="Eagle (heraldry)">
        eagle displayed
       </a>
       as single
       <a href="/wiki/Supporter" title="Supporter">
        supporter
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-suarez_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-suarez-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As queen, she
       <a href="/wiki/Quartering_(heraldry)" title="Quartering (heraldry)">
        quartered
       </a>
       the Royal Arms of the Crown of Castile with the Royal Arms of the Crown of Aragon, she and Ferdinand II of Aragon adopted a
       <a href="/wiki/Yoke_and_arrows" title="Yoke and arrows">
        yoke and a bundle of arrows
       </a>
       as
       <a href="/wiki/Heraldic_badge" title="Heraldic badge">
        heraldic badges
       </a>
       . As co-monarchs, Isabella and Ferdinand used the motto "
       <a href="/wiki/Tanto_monta,_monta_tanto,_Isabel_como_Fernando" title="Tanto monta, monta tanto, Isabel como Fernando">
        Tanto Monta
       </a>
       " (
       <i>
        "They amount to the same", or "Equal opposites in balance"
       </i>
       ), it refers their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prenuptial" title="Prenuptial">
        prenuptial
       </a>
       agreement. The conquest of
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Granada_(Crown_of_Castile)" title="Kingdom of Granada (Crown of Castile)">
        Granada
       </a>
       in 1492 was symbolised by the addition enté en point of a quarter with a pomegranate for Granada (in Spanish
       <i>
        Granada
       </i>
       means pomegranate).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
        <a href="#cite_note-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There was an uncommon variant with the Saint John the Evangelist's eagle and two lions adopted as Castilian royal supporters by
       <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Castile" title="John II of Castile">
        John II
       </a>
       , Isabella's father.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <center>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commemoration">
        Commemoration
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Commemoration">

      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic_(Spain)_-_Memorial_JK_-_Brasilia_-_DSC00387.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2582" data-file-width="2707" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic_%28Spain%29_-_Memorial_JK_-_Brasilia_-_DSC00387.JPG/200px-Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic_%28Spain%29_-_Memorial_JK_-_Brasilia_-_DSC00387.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic_%28Spain%29_-_Memorial_JK_-_Brasilia_-_DSC00387.JPG/300px-Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic_%28Spain%29_-_Memorial_JK_-_Brasilia_-_DSC00387.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic_%28Spain%29_-_Memorial_JK_-_Brasilia_-_DSC00387.JPG/400px-Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic_%28Spain%29_-_Memorial_JK_-_Brasilia_-_DSC00387.JPG 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Cross_of_the_Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic_(Spain)_-_Memorial_JK_-_Brasilia_-_DSC00387.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Grand Cross of the Order of Isabella the Catholic
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Spanish crown created the
       <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Isabella_the_Catholic" title="Order of Isabella the Catholic">
        Order of Isabella the Catholic
       </a>
       in 1815 in honor of the queen.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbian244b-4$.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="883" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Columbian244b-4%24.jpg/220px-Columbian244b-4%24.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Columbian244b-4%24.jpg/330px-Columbian244b-4%24.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Columbian244b-4%24.jpg/440px-Columbian244b-4%24.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbian244b-4$.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Queen Isabella ~ Christopher Columbus
         <center>
          <a href="/wiki/Columbian_Issue#The_$4_stamp" title="Columbian Issue">
           Issue of 1893
          </a>
         </center>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Columbian_Issue_1893-5c.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="856" data-file-width="1234" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Columbian_Issue_1893-5c.jpg/220px-Columbian_Issue_1893-5c.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Columbian_Issue_1893-5c.jpg/330px-Columbian_Issue_1893-5c.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Columbian_Issue_1893-5c.jpg/440px-Columbian_Issue_1893-5c.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Columbian_Issue_1893-5c.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         5 cent U.S. postage stamp, Columbus soliciting aid of Isabella
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Isabella was the first woman to be featured on US postage stamps,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scotts_102-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Scotts-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
       namely on three stamps of the
       <a href="/wiki/Columbian_Issue" title="Columbian Issue">
        Columbian Issue
       </a>
       , also in celebration of Columbus. She appears in the 'Columbus soliciting aid of Isabella', 5-cent issue, and on the Spanish court scene replicated on the 15-cent Columbian, and on the $4 issue, in full portrait, side by side with Columbus.
      </p>
      <p>
       The $4 stamp is the only stamp of that denomination ever issued and one which collectors prize not only for its rarity (only 30,000 were printed) but its beauty, an exquisite carmine with some copies having a crimson hue. Mint specimens of this commemorative have been sold for more than $20,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scotts-quantity_103-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Scotts-quantity-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Isabella was also the first named woman to appear on a United States coin, an 1893
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Commemorative_Coin" title="United States Commemorative Coin">
        commemorative
       </a>
       quarter, celebrating the 400th anniversary of
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">
        Columbus
       </a>
       's first voyage.
      </p>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Books">
        Books
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Books">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       A biography of Isabella is "Isabella, The Warrior Queen" by Kirsten Downey, published by Anchor Books of Penguin Random House in 2014.
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella is the subject of "The Queen's Vow" by
       <a href="/wiki/C.W._Gortner" title="C.W. Gortner">
        C.W. Gortner
       </a>
       , published in 2012.
      </p>
      <p>
       A young Isabella is the main protagonist in " Isabel, Jewel of Castile," a part of the Royal Diaries series by Scholastic.
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella's life from her early youth through the conquest of
       <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">
        Granada
       </a>
       is novelised in
       <i>
        The Queen's Cross: A biographical romance of Queen Isabella of Spain
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Schoonover" title="Lawrence Schoonover">
        Lawrence Schoonover
       </a>
       , William Sloane Associates, Inc. (New York: 1 January 1955), reprinted 1 September 2008, Fountain City Publishing,
       <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
        ISBN
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0976086743" title="Special:BookSources/0976086743">
        0976086743
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella is a main character in
       <i>
        The Prisoner of Tordesillas
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Schoonover" title="Lawrence Schoonover">
        Lawrence Schoonover
       </a>
       , Boston: Little, Brown &amp; Company; 2nd Printing edition (1959), ASIN B000P0O1DM, a novel of her daughter and successor,
       <a href="/wiki/Joanna_of_Castile" title="Joanna of Castile">
        Joanna of Castile
       </a>
       , mother of
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">
        Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella is the narrator of
       <i>
        Crown of Aloes
       </i>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Norah_Lofts" title="Norah Lofts">
        Norah Lofts
       </a>
       , Doubleday (1973) ASIN B00DY1H8TI.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">
        Video games
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isabella_I_of_Castile&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Video games">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       As the leader of the Spanish civilization in
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sid_Meier%27s_Civilization_V" title="Sid Meier's Civilization V">
         Sid Meier's Civilization V
        </a>
       </i>
       , Isabella I is depicted carrying a gilded Christian cross while standing behind a
       <a href="/wiki/Moorish_architecture" title="Moorish architecture">
        Moorish-style
       </a>
       palace likely to be the
       <a href="/wiki/Alhambra" title="Alhambra">
        Alhambra
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Isabella I is listed in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed:_Brotherhood" title="Assassin's Creed: Brotherhood">
         Assassin's Creed: Brotherhood
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assassin%27s_Creed:_Project_Legacy" title="Assassin's Creed: Project Legacy">
         Assassin's Creed: Project Legacy
        </a>
       </i>
       as a potential assassination target for the player's assassin recruits.
      </p>
      <p>
       She made an appearance in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Empires_III" title="Age of Empires III">
         Age of Empires III
        </a>
       </i>
       , where her personality can be seen when the AI plays Spain. Special dialogue has been written to reflect her personality and behavior. She was also in
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Assasin%E2%80%99s_Creed:_The_palace&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Assasin’s Creed: The palace (page does not exist)">
        Assasin’s Creed: The palace
       </a>
      </p>

         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">
        <div style="width: 182px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Socha_Izabely_I_Katolickej.JPG">
            <img alt="" data-file-height="467" data-file-width="700" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Socha_Izabely_I_Katolickej.JPG/270px-Socha_Izabely_I_Katolickej.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Socha_Izabely_I_Katolickej.JPG/405px-Socha_Izabely_I_Katolickej.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Socha_Izabely_I_Katolickej.JPG/540px-Socha_Izabely_I_Katolickej.JPG 2x" width="180"/>
           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           Statue of Isabella I the Catholic in front of the seat of the Organization of American States in Washington D.C.
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
      </ul>

        <li id="cite_note-Spanish_historian_Ana_Carrasco_Manchado_(21)-26">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-Spanish_historian_Ana_Carrasco_Manchado_(21)_26-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#Manchado">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          Spanish historian Ana Carrasco Manchado:
          <i>
           "...The battle [of Toro] was fierce and uncertain, and because of that both sides attributed themselves the victory. Prince John, the son of Alfonso of Portugal, sent letters to the Portuguese cities declaring victory. And Ferdinand of Aragon did the same. Both wanted to take advantage of the victory's propaganda."
          </i>
          In
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=qADOoHct1MwC&amp;printsec=frontcover&amp;dq=Isabel+I+de+Castilla+y+la+sombra+de+la+ilegitimidad.+Propaganda+y+representación+en+el+conflicto+sucesorio+%281474–1482%29&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=sxnzroys_j&amp;sig=aM79jFNVQ3dl8c47tP2FGbR" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Isabel I de Castilla y la sombra de la ilegitimidad: propaganda y representación en el conflicto sucesorio (1474–1482)
           </i>
          </a>
          , 2006, p. 195, 196.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-Spanish_historian_Cesáreo_Fernández_Duro_(22)-27">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-Spanish_historian_Cesáreo_Fernández_Duro_(22)_27-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Spanish_historian_Cesáreo_Fernández_Duro_(22)_27-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#Duro">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          Spanish historian Cesáreo Fernández Duro:
          <i>
           "...For those who ignore the background of these circumstances it will certainly seem strange that while the Catholic Monarchs raised a temple in Toledo in honour of the victory that God granted them on that occasion, the same fact [the Battle of Toro] was festively celebrated with solemn processions on its anniversary in Portugal"
          </i>
          in
          <a class="external text" href="http://descargas.cervantesvirtual.com/servlet/SirveObras/hist/09255096579869640757857/023863.pdf?incr=1" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            La batalla de Toro (1476). Datos y documentos para su monografía histórica
           </i>
          </a>
          , in Boletín de la Real Academia de la Historia, tome 38, Madrid, 1901,p. 250.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-Manchado_(23)-28">

          <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/pt:Vida_e_Feitos_D%27_El-Rey_Dom_Jo%C3%A3o_Segundo/XIII" title="wikisource:pt:Vida e Feitos D' El-Rey Dom João Segundo/XIII">
           <i>
            Vida e feitos d'El Rei D.João II
           </i>
          </a>

         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-Chronicler_Pulgar_(Castilian)_(26)-31">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-Chronicler_Pulgar_(Castilian)_(26)_31-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#Pulgar">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          chronicler
          <a href="/wiki/Hernando_del_Pulgar" title="Hernando del Pulgar">
           Hernando del Pulgar
          </a>
          (Castilian):
          <i>
           "...promptly, those 6 Castilian captains, which we already told were at the right side of the royal battle, and were invested by the prince of Portugal and the bishop of Évora, turned their backs and put themselves on the run."
          </i>
          in
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.cervantesvirtual.com/obra/cronica-de-los-senores-reyes-catolicos-don-fernando-y-dona-isabel-de-castilla-y-de-aragon--2/" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Crónica de los Señores Reyes Católicos Don Fernando y Doña Isabel de Castilla y de Aragón
           </i>
          </a>
          , chapter XLV.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-chronicler_Garcia_de_Resende_(Portuguese)(27)-32">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-chronicler_Garcia_de_Resende_(Portuguese)(27)_32-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#Resende">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          chronicler
          <a href="/wiki/Garcia_de_Resende" title="Garcia de Resende">
           Garcia de Resende
          </a>
          (Portuguese):
          <i>
           "... And being the battles of both sides ordered that way and prepared to attack by nearly sunshine, the King ordered the prince to attack the enemy with his and God's blessing, which he obeyed (...). (...) and after the sound of the trumpets and screaming all for S. George invested so bravely the enemy battles, and in spite of their enormous size, they could not stand the hard fight and were rapidly beaten and put on the run with great losses."
          </i>
          In

           </i>
          </a>
          , chapter XIII.
         </span>

And without discipline and with great disorder they went to Zamora. So being the Prince alone on the field without suffering defeat but inflicting it on the adversary he became heir and master of his own victory"

        <li id="cite_note-French_historian_(32)-37">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-French_historian_(32)_37-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#Dumont">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          French historian Jean Dumont in
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=rkTcRTRCSYgC&amp;pg=PA49&amp;dq=%22batalla+de+Toro+indecisa&amp;hl=pt-PT&amp;ei=coyjTumhOqLP4QSCsq3mBA&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;ct=book-thumbnail&amp;resnum=8&amp;ved=0CEsQ6wEwBzhk#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            La "imcomparable" Isabel la Catolica/ The incomparable Isabel the Catholic
           </i>
          </a>
          , Encuentro Ediciones, printed by Rogar-Fuenlabrada, Madrid, 1993 (Spanish edition), p. 49:
          <i>
           "...But in the left
          </i>
          [Portuguese]
          <i>
           Wing, in front of the Asturians and Galician, the reinforcement army of the Prince heir of Portugal, well provided with artillery, could leave the battlefield with its head high. The battle resulted this way, inconclusive. But its global result stays after that decided by the withdraw of the Portugal's King, the surrender... of the Zamora's fortress on March 19, and the multiple adhesions of the nobles to the young princes."
          </i>
         </span>

          </i>
          [Ferdinand]
          <i>
           to the main cities... are a model of skill. (...) what a powerful description of the battle! The nebulous transforms into light, the doubtful acquires the profile of a certain triumph. The politic
          </i>
          [Ferdinand]
          <i>
           achieved the fruits of a discussed victory."
          </i>

        <li id="cite_note-Vicente_Álvarez_Palenzuela_(36)-41">

            ^

          <a class="external text" href="http://www.cervantesvirtual.com/obra/la-guerra-civil-castellana-y-el-enfrentamiento-con-portugal-14751479-0/" rel="nofollow">

           </i>
          </a>
          :
          <i>
           "That is the battle of Toro. The Portuguese army had not been exactly defeated, however, the sensation was that D. Juana's cause had completely sunk. It made sense that for the Castilians Toro was considered as the divine retribution, the compensation desired by God to compensate the terrible disaster of
           <a href="/wiki/Aljubarrota" title="Aljubarrota">

           </a>
           , still alive in the Castilian memory"
          </i>
          .

        <li id="cite_note-45">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-45">

        <li id="cite_note-Battle_of_Guinea_(40)-46">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-Battle_of_Guinea_(40)_46-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-Battle_of_Guinea_(40)_46-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guinea" title="Battle of Guinea">
           Battle of Guinea
          </a>
          :
          <a href="#Palencia">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          Alonso de Palencia,
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=-1A3cWT_1kAC&amp;pg=PA93&amp;lpg=PA93&amp;dq=%22Alonso+de+Palencia+decada+cuarta+naves+castellanas%22&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=kdDs0IZIC2&amp;sig=1GhLLlK7uT95iMhwkS2KqoLeBJQ&amp;hl=pt-PT&amp;ei=zGpZTbrYFIKAhQf-9YyDDQ&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;ct=result&amp;resnum=1&amp;ved" rel="nofollow">
           Década IV
          </a>
          , Book XXXIII, Chapter V (
          <i>
           "Disaster among those sent to the mines of gold
          </i>
          [Guinea]
          <i>
           . Charges against the King..."
          </i>
          ), pp. 91–94. This was a decisive battle because after it, in spite of the Catholic Monarchs' attempts, they were unable to send new fleets to Guinea, Canary or to any part of the Portuguese empire until the end of the war. The
          <a href="/wiki/John_II_of_Portugal" title="John II of Portugal">
           <i>
            Perfect Prince
           </i>
          </a>
          sent an order to drown any Castilian crew captured in Guinea waters. Even the Castilian navies which left Guinea before the signature of the peace treaty had to pay the tax ("quinto") to the Portuguese crown when they returned to Castile after the peace treaty. Isabella had to ask permission of Afonso V so that this tax could be paid in Castilian harbours. Naturally all this caused a grudge against the Catholic Monarchs in Andalusia.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-Historian_Malyn_Newitt-47">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-Historian_Malyn_Newitt_47-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#Newitt">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          Historian Malyn Newitt:
          <i>
           "However, in 1478 the Portuguese surprised thirty-five Castilian ships returning from Mina
          </i>
          [Guinea]
          <i>
           and seized them and all their gold. Another...Castilian voyage to Mina, that of
           <a href="/wiki/Eustache_de_la_Fosse" title="Eustache de la Fosse">
            Eustache de la Fosse
           </a>
           , was intercepted ... in 1480. (...) All things considered, it is not surprising that the Portuguese emerged victorious from this
           <b>
            first maritime colonial war
           </b>
           . They were far better organised than the Castilians, were able to raise money for the preparation and supply of their fleets, and had clear central direction from ...
          </i>
          [Prince]
          <i>
           John."
          </i>
          In
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.google.com/search?q=%22the+Portuguese+emerged+victorious+from+this+first+maritime+colonial+war.%22+&amp;btnG=Pesquisar+livros&amp;tbm=bks&amp;tbo=1&amp;hl=pt-PT" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            A history of Portuguese overseas expansion, 1400–1668
           </i>
          </a>
          , Routledge, New York, 2005, pp. 39–40.
         </span>
        </li>

         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

          </i>

          </a>
          , volume I, University of Minnesota Press, 1985,
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.google.com/search?q=%22In+a+war+in+which+the+Castilians+were+victorious+on+land+and+the+Portuguese+at+sea%22&amp;btnG=Pesquisar+livros&amp;tbm=bks&amp;tbo=1&amp;hl=pt-PT" rel="nofollow">
           p. 152
          </a>
          .
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-50">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-50">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          :
          <a href="#Palencia">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          Alonso de Palencia,
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=-1A3cWT_1kAC&amp;pg=PA93&amp;lpg=PA93&amp;dq=%22Alonso+de+Palencia+decada+cuarta+naves+castellanas%22&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=kdDs0IZIC2&amp;sig=1GhLLlK7uT95iMhwkS2KqoLeBJQ&amp;hl=pt-PT&amp;ei=zGpZTbrYFIKAhQf-9YyDDQ&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;ct=result&amp;resnum=1&amp;ved" rel="nofollow">
           Decada IV
          </a>
          , Book XXXI, Chapters VIII and IX (
          <i>
           "preparation of 2 fleets
          </i>
          [to Guinea and to Canary, respectively]
          <i>
           so that with them King Ferdinand crush its enemies
          </i>
          [the Portuguese]..."
          <i>
           ).
          </i>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-Alonso_de_Palencia_(44)-51">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-Alonso_de_Palencia_(44)_51-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#Palencia">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          Alonso de Palencia,
          <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=-1A3cWT_1kAC&amp;pg=PA93&amp;lpg=PA93&amp;dq=%22Alonso+de+Palencia+decada+cuarta+naves+castellanas%22&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=kdDs0IZIC2&amp;sig=1GhLLlK7uT95iMhwkS2KqoLeBJQ&amp;hl=pt-PT&amp;ei=zGpZTbrYFIKAhQf-9YyDDQ&amp;sa=X&amp;oi=book_result&amp;ct=result&amp;resnum=1&amp;ved" rel="nofollow">
           Decada IV
          </a>
          , book XXXII, chapter III: in 1478 a Portuguese fleet intercepted the armada of 25 navies sent by Ferdinand to conquer Gran Canary – capturing 5 of its navies plus 200 Castilians – and forced it to fled hastily and definitively from Canary waters. This victory allowed Prince John to use the Canary Islands as an "exchange coin" in the peace treaty of Alcáçovas.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-52">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-52">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#Pina">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          Pina,
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/files/24508/24508-h/24508-h.htm" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Chronica de El-Rei D. Affonso V
           </i>
          </a>
          , 3rd book, chapter CXCIV (Editorial error: Chapter CXCIV erroneously appears as Chapter CLXIV.Reports the end of the siege of Ceuta by the arrival of the fleet with Afonso V).
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-53">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-53">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#Quesada">
           <sub>
            <big>
             ↓
            </big>
           </sub>
          </a>
          Quesada,
          <a class="external text" href="http://revistas.ucm.es/index.php/ELEM/article/view/ELEM0000110067A/22548" rel="nofollow">
           <i>
            Portugueses en la frontera de Granada
           </i>
          </a>
          , 2000, p. 98. In 1476 Ceuta was simultaneously besieged by the moors and a Castilian army led by the Duke of Medina Sidónia. The Castilians conquered the city from the Portuguese who took refuge in the inner fortress, but a Portuguese fleet arrived
          <i>
           "in extremis"
          </i>
          and regained the city. A Ceuta dominated by the Castilians would certainly have forced the right to conquer Fez (Morocco) to be shared between Portugal and Castile instead of the monopoly the Portuguese acquired.
         </span>
        </li>

          ISSN
         </a>
         :
         <a class="external text" href="http://bddoc.csic.es:8080/detalles.html;isessionid=A31394B29A781B0B063B6993FDA9FAEE?id=30676&amp;bd=HISTORI&amp;tabla=docu" rel="nofollow">
          0210-6310
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>

         <i>
          Gesta Hispaniensia ex annalibus suorum diebus colligentis, Década III

           and IV
